Three Aspects of Conceptual Knowledge in Logic
Author enumerates the three aspects of conceptual knowledge that logic investigates.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and distinguish the three aspects of conceptual knowledge that logic investigates.

Core Idea
Logic examines not only how definitions are built but also the universal attributes and subject-predicate structure they depend on.

This passage outlines the three dimensions of conceptual knowledge that fall within the subject matter of logic. Understanding these dimensions helps clarify how logic connects conceptual composition, the attributes of universals, and the propositional structure that supports reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first aspect – composition
The first aspect is the composition of two known conceptuals, like genus and differentia, to form a definition of an unknown conceptual. For example, 'animal' and 'rational' compose to define 'human'. Similarly, two propositions compose to form a syllogism.
2
Identify the second aspect – proximate dependencies
The second aspect is the direct dependence on attributes of the conceptual knowns: universality, particularity, essentiality, accidentalness, genus, differentia, and property. These are studied in the chapter on the five universals.
The mention of particularity here is a digression.
3
Identify the third aspect – remote dependencies
The third aspect is the indirect dependence on subjects and predicates, which are conceptual knowns that form the propositions. This is investigated within the chapter on propositions.
4
Recognise the logical progression
The three aspects form a logical progression: from the actual composition, to the attributes that enable the composition, to the syntactic roles (subject/predicate) that underlie the composition. This structure shows how logic systematically treats conceptual knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
موضوع المنطق: عن الجنس - كالحيوان - والفصل - كالناطق - وهما معلومان تصوریان من حيث أنهما كيف يركبان ليوصل المجموع إلى مجهول تصوّري كالإنسان، وكما يبحث عن القضايا المتعدّدة، كقولنا : «العالم متغير وكل متغير محدث وهما معلومان تصديقيان من حيث أنهما كيف يؤلفان، فيصير المجموع قياساً موصلاً إلى مجهول تصديقي، كقولنا : «العالم محدث» وثانيها ما يتوقف عليه الإيصال إلى المجهول التصوري، توقفاً قريباً، ككون المعلومات التصورية كليّة وجزئية، وذاتية وعرضيّة، وجنساً وفصلاً وخاصة فإن الموصل إلى التصور يتركب من هذه الأمور، فالإيصال يتوقف على هذه الأحوال بلاواسطة، فذكر الجزئية هاهنا على سبيل الاستطراد والبحث عن هذه الأحوال في باب الكليات الخمس. وثالثها ما يتوقف عليه الإيصال إلى المجهول التصديقي توقفاً بعيداً، أي بواسطة، ككون المعلومات التصورية موضوعات ومحمولات، والبحث عنها في ضمن باب القضايا.
The subject of logic: concerning genus - like animal - and differentia - like rational - and they are two conceptual knowns in terms of how they are combined to make the composite reach an unknown conceptual, like human. And similarly it investigates multiple propositions, like our statement: 'The world is changing and every changing thing is temporally originated' and they are two assents knowns in terms of how they are composed so that the composite becomes a syllogism reaching an unknown assent, like our statement: 'The world is temporally originated'. Second: that upon which the reaching to the unknown conceptual depends, proximately, like the conceptual knowns being universal and particular, essential and accidental, genus and differentia and property; for the thing that reaches to conceptual is composed of these matters, so the reaching depends on these states without intermediary. Mentioning particularity here is by way of digression, and the investigation of these states is in the chapter of the five universals. Third: that upon which the reaching to the unknown assent depends remotely, i.e., through an intermediary, like the conceptual knowns being subjects and predicates, and its investigation is within the chapter of propositions.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage classifies the three aspects of conceptual knowledge that fall within the subject matter of logic. The first aspect is the composition itself: how two known conceptuals (genus and differentia) combine to produce a definition of an unknown conceptual (e.g., 'human' from 'animal' and 'rational'). The same structure applies to assent: two known propositions combine into a syllogism to yield an unknown assent (e.g., 'The world is temporally originated' from 'The world is changing' and 'Everything changing is temporally originated'). The second aspect is the proximate dependencies: the conceptual knowns must be understood in terms of their universality, particularity, essentiality, accidentalness, genus, differentia, and property, because the definition is composed of these elements. These are investigated in the chapter on the five universals. The third aspect is the remote dependencies: the subjects and predicates that make up propositions, which are themselves composed of conceptual knowns. Thus logic examines these three levels for conceptual knowledge.

The Subject Matter of Logic: Essential Accidents
Author summarizes that logic studies the essential attributes of conceptual and assent information.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain what 'essential accidents' (al-aʿrāḍ al-dhātiyya) are and identify the two broad categories of information that logic investigates.

Core Idea
Logic studies the essential accidents of information, not the essences of things.

This passage summarizes the entire subject matter of logic. The author explains that logic investigates the states of conceptual and assent information that enable us to reach unknown knowledge. These states are called 'essential accidents' because they belong to information by virtue of its role in reasoning, not from external factors. Let's break down this core concept.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of information
The passage distinguishes between conceptual information (tasawwurāt) and assent information (taṣdīqāt). Conceptual information is the raw material of definitions; assent information is the raw material of syllogisms.
This division is fundamental in Islamic logic.
2
Find the attributes investigated for each type
For conceptual information, logic investigates whether it is universal or particular, essential or accidental, and whether it serves as genus, differentia, or property. For assent information, logic investigates propositions, their converses, and contradictories (proximate), and subjects and predicates (remote).
These attributes are called 'essential accidents' because they are inseparable from the role of information in reaching the unknown.
3
Understand proximate vs. remote dependency
Assent information depends on propositions directly (proximately) and on subjects and predicates indirectly (remotely), because propositions are composed of subjects and predicates.
This distinction clarifies the layers of logical analysis.
4
Define 'essential accident'
The passage concludes that the logician is an investigator of the essential accidents (aʿrāḍ dhātiyya) of conceptual and assent information. These are attributes that belong to information in itself, not by external causes.
The Arabic term 'dhātiyya' indicates that these accidents are intrinsic to the nature of information as a tool for knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذلك يبحث عنها من حيث أنها يتوقف عليها الموصل إلى التصور، ككون المعلومات التصورية كلية وجزئية، وذاتية وعرضية، وجنسا وفصلا وخاصة، ومن حيث أنها يتوقف عليها الموصل إلى التصديق، إما توقفا قريبا - أي بلاواسطة - ككون المعلومات التصديقية قضية أو عكس قضية أو نقيض قضية - وإما توقفا بعيدا – أي بواسطة، ككونها موضوعات ومحمولات - فإن الموصل إلى التصديق يتوقف على القضايا بالذات لتركبه منها، والقضايا موقوفة على الموضوعات والمحمولات فيكون الموصل إلى التصديق موقوفا على القضايا بالذات، وعلى الموضوعات والمحمولات بواسطة توقف القضايا عليها. وبالجملة، المنطقي يبحث عن أحوال المعلومات التصورية والتصديقية التي هي إما نفس الإيصال إلى المجهولات، أو الأحوال التي يتوقف عليها الإيصال، وهذه الأحوال عارضة للمعلومات التصورية والتصديقية لذواتها، فهو باحث عن الأعراض الذاتية لها.
And likewise it investigates them insofar as the thing that reaches to the conceptual depends on them, like the conceptual information being universal and particular, essential and accidental, genus and differentia and property; and insofar as the thing that reaches to the assent depends on them, either proximately – i.e., without intermediary – like the assent information being a proposition or the converse of a proposition or the contradictory of a proposition; or remotely – i.e., through an intermediary – like them being subjects and predicates. For the thing that reaches to assent depends on propositions essentially because it is composed of them, and propositions depend on subjects and predicates; so the thing that reaches to assent depends on propositions essentially, and on subjects and predicates through the intermediary of the dependence of propositions on them. In summary, the logician investigates the states of conceptual and assent information which are either the very reaching to the unknowns, or the states upon which the reaching depends; and these states are accidental to conceptual and assent information in themselves, so he is an investigator of their essential accidents.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage summarizes the entire subject matter of logic. The logician examines conceptual information both as the basis for definitions (e.g., universality, essentialness, genus, differentia, property) and as the remote components of propositions (subjects and predicates). For assent information, he examines propositions themselves (proximate dependence) and their converses and contradictories, as well as subjects and predicates (remote dependence). The key point is that logic studies the essential accidents (aʿrāḍ dhātiyya) of these information types – attributes that belong to them by virtue of their role in leading to the unknown.

Key Terms
الأعراض الذاتية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does the logician investigate subjects and predicates?
A) As proximate dependents of assent.
B) As remote dependents of assent.
C) As direct conceptual information.
D) As essential definitions.

Key Takeaway
Logic investigates the essential accidents of both conceptual and assent information because these are the tools for reaching unknown knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify whether 'essential' and 'accidental' as applied to information are themselves essential accidents or just accidental descriptions. Use the passage's definition.

Attributes of Conceptual and Assent Information
Author enumerates attributes of conceptual and assent information.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the specific attributes of conceptual information that logic studies and distinguish them from the attributes of assent information.

Core Idea
Logic studies how conceptual information is categorized and how assent information is structured.

The author provides a detailed enumeration: conceptual information is examined for being universal or particular, essential or accidental, and as genus, differentia, or property. Assent information is examined for being propositions, their converses, contradictories, and their remote components (subjects and predicates). This lesson unpacks each category to see how they serve as tools for reaching the unknown.

Guided Path
1
Extract the attributes of conceptual information
From the passage: universal (kulliyya) vs. particular (juz'iyya), essential (dhātiyya) vs. accidental ('araḍiyya), and genus (jins), differentia (fasl), property (khāṣṣa). These are the essential accidents that enable definitions.
These correspond to the five universals (al-kulliyyāt al-khams) in logica.
2
Extract the attributes of assent information
Proximate: proposition (qaḍiyya), its converse ('aks), its contradictory (naqīḍ). Remote: subject (mawḍū‘) and predicate (maḥmūl). These are the essential accidents that enable syllogisms.
Remote attributes are studied through the mediation of propositions.
3
Understand the relevance of each attribute
Each attribute is an 'essential accident' because it is inseparable from the information's role in reasoning. For example, a proposition must have truth-value; its converse and contradictory are immediate transformations.
Without these attributes, information could not serve as a premise or definition.

The Subject Matter of Logic: Conceptual and Assertive Knowledge
Author defines logic's subject matter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the subject matter of logic as the study of the essential accidents of conceptual and assertive knowledge that lead to the unknown.

Core Idea
Logic studies only the essential accidents of conceptual and assertive knowledge that guide us to the unknown.

Logic is not about everything in the mind. It focuses specifically on the conditions that help us move from known concepts and judgments to the unknown. This passage from Qutbi defines logic's subject matter as the investigation of conceptual (tasawwur) and assertive (tasdiq) information, focusing on the essential accidents that make conveyance possible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of information in logic
Look for the terms tasawwur (تصوّر) and tasdiq (تصديق) in the Arabic. These are the two types of knowledge that logic studies.
2
Distinguish the conditions for each category
For conceptual knowledge, logic studies properties like universality, particularity, essentiality, accidentalness, genus, differentia, and property. For assertive knowledge, it studies conditions of propositions, their converses, contradictions, and subjects/predicates.
3
Understand the types of dependence for assertive knowledge
The passage distinguishes immediate dependence (direct properties of propositions) from mediate dependence (subjects and predicates that propositions depend on).
4
Recognize the concept of essential accidents (a'rad dhatiyya)
The passage states that the logician investigates the states that are accidental but essential to conceptual and assertive information, i.e., properties that belong to them by virtue of their essence.
5
Summarize the subject matter of logic
Logic investigates the essential accidents of conceptual and assertive knowledge that are either the means to the unknown or the states upon which those means depend.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذلك يبحث عنها من حيث أنها يتوقف عليها الموصل إلى التصوّر، ككون المعلومات التصورية كليّة وجزئية، وذاتية وعرضية، وجنساً وفصلاً وخاصةً، ومن حيث أنها يتوقف عليها الموصل إلى التصديق، إما توقفا قريباً - أي بلاواسطة - ككون المعلومات التصديقية قضية أو عكس قضيّة أو نقيض قضيّة - وإما توقفا بعيداً – أي بواسطة، ككونها موضوعات ومحمولات - فإنّ الموصل إلى التصديق يتوقف على القضايا بالذات لتركبه منها، والقضايا موقوفة على الموضوعات والمحمولات فيكون الموصل إلى التصديق موقوفاً على القضايا بالذات ، وعلى الموضوعات والمحمولات بواسطة توقف القضايا عليها.
وبالجملة، المنطقي يبحث عن أحوال المعلومات التصورية والتصديقية التي هي إما نفس الإيصال إلى المجهولات، أو الأحوال التي يتوقف عليها الإيصال ، وهذه الأحوال عارضة للمعلومات التصورية والتصديقية لذواتها، فهو باحث عن الأعراض الذاتية لها.
(1) إشارة إلى الإيصال والأحوال التي يتوقف عليها الإيصال معاً (شريف).
And likewise, it investigates it in terms of what the conveyance to conceptualization depends upon, such as conceptual information being universal and particular, essential and accidental, genus, differentia, and property; and in terms of what the conveyance to assent depends upon: either immediate dependence—i.e., without mediation—such as assertive information being a proposition, or the converse of a proposition, or the contradictory of a proposition; or mediate dependence—i.e., with mediation—such as them being subjects and predicates. For the conveyance to assent depends essentially on propositions because it is composed of them, and propositions depend on subjects and predicates. Thus the conveyance to assent depends on propositions essentially, and on subjects and predicates mediatedly due to the dependence of propositions on them. In summary, the logician investigates the states of conceptual and assertive information that are either the conveyance itself to the unknowns, or the states upon which conveyance depends. And these states are accidents of conceptual and assertive information in themselves, so he is an investigator of their essential accidents. (1) Reference to conveyance and the states upon which conveyance depends together (Sharif).
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage defines the subject matter of logic (mantiq). The author explains that logic investigates conceptual (tasawwur) and assertive (tasdiq) information from two perspectives: first, the conditions upon which the means leading to conceptual knowledge depend—such as the universality or particularity, essentiality or accidentalness, or being genus, differentia, or property of concepts; second, the conditions upon which the means leading to assertive knowledge depend, either immediately (e.g., being a proposition, its converse, or its contradictory) or mediatedly (e.g., being subjects or predicates). The author then clarifies that the conveyance to assent (al-muwassil ila al-tasdiq) depends essentially on propositions, and propositions in turn depend on subjects and predicates. In summary, the logician examines the states of conceptual and assertive information that are either the very means of conveying to the unknown or the conditions on which that conveyance depends. These states are accidental (aradi) to their subjects but essential accidents (a'rad dhatiyya) in the sense that they belong to the subject qua subject. Thus logic studies the essential accidents of conceptual and assertive knowledge.

Key Terms
تصوّر
تصديق
أعراض ذاتية

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Propositions (qadaya)
C) Subjects and predicates directly

Key Takeaway
Logic's subject matter is the study of the essential accidents of conceptual and assertive knowledge that lead to the unknown, not all aspects of thought.

The Three Types of Word Indication
Author defines the three types of indication.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three types of indication (mutabaqa, tadammun, iltizam) and identify each in an Islamic term.

Core Idea
A word indicates its full meaning, a part, or a necessary concomitant.

Words are not the logician's primary focus, but they are the vehicle for conveying meanings. Before diving into the logician's true subject matter, the author defines three ways a word can indicate its meaning: fully (mutabaqa), partially (tadammun), or by implication (iltizam). Understanding these distinctions is essential for analyzing definitions and arguments in any Islamic science.

Guided Path
1
Extract the definitions
From the passage, identify the three types: mutabaqa (full indication), tadammun (partial indication), and iltizam (implied indication). Note that each is defined by its relation to the meaning for which the word was coined.
Mutabaqa corresponds to the entire meaning; tadammun to a part; iltizam to something external but necessarily attached.
2
Analyze the given example
The word 'insan' (human) indicates 'rational animal' (hayawan natiq) as mutabaqa; 'animal' alone or 'rational' alone as tadammun; and 'receptive of knowledge and writing' as iltizam. Ensure you see how each fits the definition.
3
Apply to an Islamic term
Take the term 'salat'. What does it indicate as mutabaqa? (the ritual prayer). As tadammun? (any of its pillars like ruku). As iltizam? (obligation or validity conditions). This mirrors the passage's method.
The examples must come from an Islamic science, not a secular one.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الأول دلالة المطابقة والتضمن والإلتزام. في الألفاظ دلالة اللفظ على المعنى بتوسّط الوضع له «مطابقة» كدلالة «الإنسان» على «الحيوان الناطق»؛ وبتوسّطه لما دخل فيه ذلك المعنى «تضمن» كدلالته على «الحيوان»، وعلى «الناطق» فقط ؛ ويتوسطه لما خرج عنه «التزام» كدلالته على «قابل العلم وصنعة الكتابة». أقول : لا شغل للمنطقي - من حيث هو منطقي - بالألفاظ، فإنّه يبحث عن القول الشارح والحجّة وكيفية ترتيبهما، وهو لا يتوقف على الألفاظ، فإن ما يوصل إلى التصوّر ليس لفظ «الجنس» و«الفصل» بـل معناهما، وكذلك ما يوصل إلى التصديق مفهومات القضايا لا ألفاظها، ولكن لما توقف إفادة المعاني واستفادتها على الألفاظ صار النظر فيها مقصوداً بالعرض وبالقصد الثاني
The first chapter: Indication of مطابقة, تضمن, and التزام. Regarding words: The indication of a word upon a meaning by virtue of its being put for it is 'مطابقة' [full indication], like the indication of 'human' upon 'rational animal'; and by virtue of it [the word] indicating what is included in that meaning is 'تضمن' [partial indication], like its indication upon 'animal' alone, and upon 'rational' alone; and by virtue of it indicating what is outside it is 'التزام' [implied indication], like its indication upon 'receptive of knowledge and the craft of writing.' I say: The logician, qua logician, has no concern with words, because he investigates the explanatory statement (al-qawl al-sharih) and the proof (al-hujja) and how to arrange them, and that does not depend on words. For what leads to conceptualization (tasawwur) is not the word 'genus' or 'difference' but their meanings; and similarly, what leads to assent (tasdiq) are the concepts of propositions, not their words. However, because the communication and reception of meanings depend on words, consideration of them becomes intended secondarily and by secondary intention.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage is a definitional passage from the Sharh explaining the three types of indication (دلالة). The author first defines each type with an example from the word 'human' (إنسان). مطابقة is when the word indicates the entire meaning for which it was coined; here 'human' indicates 'rational animal' (الحيوان الناطق), its complete definition. تضمن is when the word indicates a part of that meaning; 'human' indicates 'animal' individually or 'rational' individually. التزام is when the word indicates something external to the meaning but necessarily associated; 'human' indicates 'receptive of knowledge and writing' — a concomitant property. Then the commentator adds a note: the logician as such is not concerned with words themselves, but with meanings. However, because conveying meanings requires words, the logician studies them secondarily. This is an important methodological clarification distinguishing the logician from the grammarian. For instance, the word 'salat' in fiqh indicates the ritual prayer (مطابقة), its constituent parts like bowing (تضمن), and its obligation (التزام).

Key Terms
مطابقة
تضمن
التزام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, the word 'human' indicating 'animal' alone is an example of which type of indication?
A) مطابقة
B) تضمن
C) التزام
D) None

Key Takeaway
A single word can indicate its meaning in three distinct ways: the full meaning, a part, or a necessary concomitant.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify the type of indication for the word 'zakat' in the phrase 'wa atu al-zakat': mutabaqa (the obligatory alms), tadammun (the act of giving), or iltizam (purity)? Explain your reasoning.
?
Construct a similar three-way analysis for the term 'iman' (faith) using an example from kalam.

The Logician's Secondary Concern with Words
Commentator clarifies the logician's secondary relation to words.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the logician studies words only secondarily, and distinguish this from the grammarian's primary focus.

Core Idea
The logician's subject is meaning, not words; words are mere vehicles.

After defining the three types of indication, the commentator inserts an important methodological caveat: the logician (mantiqi) as such does not primarily deal with words. His real concern is the explanatory statement (qawl sharh) and proof (hujja). But because meanings cannot be communicated without words, he studies them indirectly. This clarification prevents the student from confusing logic with grammar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim
Find the sentence: 'لا شغل للمنطقي - من حيث هو منطقي - بالألفاظ'. This is the core claim: the logician qua logician has no concern with words.
This does not mean words are irrelevant, but that they are not the primary subject.
2
Find the justification
The commentator argues that the logician studies the explanatory statement (al-qawl al-sharih) and proof (al-hujja), and these do not depend on words. What matters are meanings, not the specific terms.
Conceptualization (tasawwur) comes through meanings of 'genus' and 'difference', not the words themselves.
3
Understand the qualification
However, the commentator adds: 'لما توقف إفادة المعاني واستفادتها على الألفاظ صار النظر فيها مقصوداً بالعرض' – because communicating meanings depends on words, words become a secondary concern.
So words are studied 'by secondary intention' (bi al-qasd al-thani).
4
Relate to Islamic sciences
In usul al-fiqh, a jurist (faqih) is primarily concerned with the legal rule (hukm), not the specific wording of the proof-text, but he must study wording to derive the rule. Similarly, the logician studies words only as tools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الأول دلالة المطابقة والتضمن والإلتزام. في الألفاظ دلالة اللفظ على المعنى بتوسّط الوضع له «مطابقة» كدلالة «الإنسان» على «الحيوان الناطق»؛ وبتوسّطه لما دخل فيه ذلك المعنى «تضمن» كدلالته على «الحيوان»، وعلى «الناطق» فقط ؛ ويتوسطه لما خرج عنه «التزام» كدلالته على «قابل العلم وصنعة الكتابة». أقول : لا شغل للمنطقي - من حيث هو منطقي - بالألفاظ، فإنّه يبحث عن القول الشارح والحجّة وكيفية ترتيبهما، وهو لا يتوقف على الألفاظ، فإن ما يوصل إلى التصوّر ليس لفظ «الجنس» و«الفصل» بـل معناهما، وكذلك ما يوصل إلى التصديق مفهومات القضايا لا ألفاظها، ولكن لما توقف إفادة المعاني واستفادتها على الألفاظ صار النظر فيها مقصوداً بالعرض وبالقصد الثاني
The first chapter: Indication of مطابقة, تضمن, and التزام. Regarding words: The indication of a word upon a meaning by virtue of its being put for it is 'مطابقة' [full indication], like the indication of 'human' upon 'rational animal'; and by virtue of it [the word] indicating what is included in that meaning is 'تضمن' [partial indication], like its indication upon 'animal' alone, and upon 'rational' alone; and by virtue of it indicating what is outside it is 'التزام' [implied indication], like its indication upon 'receptive of knowledge and the craft of writing.' I say: The logician, qua logician, has no concern with words, because he investigates the explanatory statement (al-qawl al-sharih) and the proof (al-hujja) and how to arrange them, and that does not depend on words. For what leads to conceptualization (tasawwur) is not the word 'genus' or 'difference' but their meanings; and similarly, what leads to assent (tasdiq) are the concepts of propositions, not their words. However, because the communication and reception of meanings depend on words, consideration of them becomes intended secondarily and by secondary intention.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage is a definitional passage from the Sharh explaining the three types of indication (دلالة). The author first defines each type with an example from the word 'human' (إنسان). مطابقة is when the word indicates the entire meaning for which it was coined; here 'human' indicates 'rational animal' (الحيوان الناطق), its complete definition. تضمن is when the word indicates a part of that meaning; 'human' indicates 'animal' individually or 'rational' individually. التزام is when the word indicates something external to the meaning but necessarily associated; 'human' indicates 'receptive of knowledge and writing' — a concomitant property. Then the commentator adds a note: the logician as such is not concerned with words themselves, but with meanings. However, because conveying meanings requires words, the logician studies them secondarily. This is an important methodological clarification distinguishing the logician from the grammarian. For instance, the word 'salat' in fiqh indicates the ritual prayer (مطابقة), its constituent parts like bowing (تضمن), and its obligation (التزام).

الحجّة

بالعرض
بالقصد الثاني

A) Words and their indications

D) The three types of indication

Key Takeaway
The logician studies words only because meanings cannot be communicated without them; his true focus is the structure of definitions and arguments.

Definition and Division of Indication (Dalalah)
Author defines indication and divides it into verbal and non-verbal types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two components (dal and madlul) in any act of indication and classify the indication as verbal or non-verbal based on the type of indicator.

Core Idea
Indication is a relation of necessary knowledge: knowing one thing forces knowledge of another.

This passage lays the foundational concept of dalalah, the core relationship that drives logical inference. Before logic can analyse arguments, it must first understand how signs (indications) work. Here we learn the precise definition and the essential division into verbal and non-verbal types, which sets the stage for studying linguistic signs in logic.

Guided Path
1
Locate the definiendum
Find the term being defined in the Arabic. It is 'الدلالة' (al-dalalah). The author states its definition clearly.
2
Extract the defining condition
The definition is: 'كون الشيء بحالة يلزم من العلم به العلم بشيء آخر' — the thing being in such a state that knowledge of it necessitates knowledge of something else.
This is a relational definition; it ties two items together.
3
Identify the two relata
The first thing (the indicator) is called الدال (al-dal), and the second (the indicated) is المدلول (al-madlul). In any act of indication, you must be able to identify both.
4
Classify the indication
The author divides indication into two types: verbal (لفظية) if the indicator is a word, and non-verbal (غير لفظية) otherwise. Non-verbal examples include script, knots, gestures, and signs.
This division is crucial because logic primarily deals with verbal indications, but the definition covers all signs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولما كان النظر فيها من حيث أنها دلائل المعاني قدم الكلام في الدلالة؛ وهي كون الشيء بحالة يلزم من العلم به العلم بشيء آخر، والشيء الأول هو الدال، والثاني هو المدلول. والدالّ إن كان لفظاً فالدلالة لفظية، وإلا فغير لفظية - كدلالة الخط (۲ والعقد والإشارات والنصب.
And since the investigation (in logic) concerns meanings (ma'ani) as indicators (dala'il) of concepts, so (the author) first discussed indication (dalalah) which is: the thing being in a state such that knowledge of it necessitates knowledge of something else. The first thing is the indicator (dal), and the second is the indicated (madlul). And the indicator if it is a word, then the indication is verbal (lafziyyah), otherwise it is non-verbal (ghayr lafziyyah), like the indication of script, knots, gestures, and signs.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage defines the fundamental concept of dalalah (indication) which is central to logic. The author explains that indication is a relationship: if you know one thing, you necessarily know another. The first is the 'dal' (signifier) and the second is the 'madlul' (signified). Then he divides indication into two types: verbal and non-verbal. Non-verbal examples include script (khat), knots ('uqad) used for counting, gestures (isharat), and signs (nasb) like road signs. This division is essential because logic deals with verbal indications as the tools of reasoning.

Key Takeaway
Dalalah is the necessary link between the indicator (dal) and the indicated (madlul), and it is divided into verbal and non-verbal types, with logic primarily concerned with the former.

The Three Types of Linguistic Signification: Mutabaqa, Tadammun, Iltizam
Qutbi defines the three types of linguistic signification with Islamic examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which type of linguistic signification (mutabaqa, tadammun, iltizam) is at work in a given Islamic example.

Core Idea
A word signifies its meaning in three ways: exact match, part inclusion, or necessary implication.

In Islamic logic, words are assigned meanings by convention (wad'). The relationship between the word and its meaning can be exact correspondence (mutabaqa), inclusion of a part (tadammun), or necessary implication (iltizam). Understanding these distinctions is essential for analyzing definitions and arguments in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the word's assigned meaning
Determine the conventional meaning for which the word was originally placed (wad'). For example, 'human' is assigned to 'rational animal'.
This is the reference point for comparison.
2
Identify the actual signified meaning in context
What does the word actually refer to in the given utterance? For instance, 'human' might refer to 'animal' in a particular context.
This is the meaning being conveyed.
3
Compare the signified meaning to the assigned meaning
Check if the signified meaning is exactly the assigned meaning (whole), a part of it, or something external but necessarily implied by it.
This comparison determines the type.
4
Classify the signification type
If the signified meaning is the whole assigned meaning → mutabaqa; if it is a part → tadammun; if it is an external necessary concomitant → iltizam.
Use the example of 'human' signifying 'rational animal' (mutabaqa), 'animal' (tadammun), or 'capable of knowledge' (iltizam).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مباحث الألفاظ
متى أطلق ) فهم منه معناه للعلم بوضعه"، وهي إما مطابقة أو تضمن أو التزام :
وذلك لأن اللفظ إذا كان دالاً بحسب الوضع على معنى، فذلك المعنى الذي هو مدلول اللفظ، إما أن يكون عين المعنى الموضوع له أو داخلاً فيه أو خارجاً عنه :
فدلالة اللفظ على معناه بواسطة أن اللفظ موضوع لذلك المعنى مطابقة، كدلالة الإنسان» على «الحيوان الناطق»، فإن الإنسان انما يدل على الحيوان الناطق لأجل أنه موضوع للحيوان الناطق.
و دلالته على معناه بواسطة أن اللفظ موضوع لمعنى داخل فيه ذلك المعنى المدلول للفظ تضمّن كدلالة «الإنسان» على «الحيوان» أو «الناطق» فإن الإنسان انما يدلّ على الحيوان أو الناطق لأجل أنه موضوع «للحيوان الناطق» وهو معنى دخل فيه «الحيوان» الذي هو مدلول اللفظ.
ودلالته على معناه بواسطة أن اللفظ موضوع لمعنى خرج عنه ذلك المعنى المدلول التزام كدلالة «الإنسان» على «قابل العلم وصنعة الكتابة» فإن دلالته عليه بواسطة أن اللفظ موضوع للحيوان الناطق» و «قابل العلم وصنعة الكتابة» خارج عنه.
أما تسمية الدلالة الأولى بالمطابقة : فلأن اللفظ مطابق – أي موافق : لتمام ما وضع له - من قولهم : طابق النعل بالنعل» إذا توافقا.
وأما تسمية الدلالة الثانية بالتضمّن : فلأن جزء المعنى الموضوع له داخل في ضمنه، فهي دلالة على مافي ضمن المعنى الموضوع له.
وأما تسمية الدلالة الثالثة بالالتزام : فلأن اللفظ لا يدل على كل أمر خارج عن معناه الموضوع له، بل على الخارج اللازم له.
و إنما قيد حدود الدلالات الثلاث بتوسط الوضع، لأنه لو لم يقيد به لانتقض حدّ بعض الدلالات ببعضها، وذلك لجواز أن يكون اللفظ مشتركاً بين الجزء و الكلّ كالإمكان، فإنّه موضوع للإمكان الخاص - و هو سلب الضرورة عن الطرفين - وللإمكان العام، وأن يكون اللفظ مشتركا بين الملزوم واللازم - كالشمس فإنه موضوع للجرم والضوء .
ويتصور من ذلك صور أربع :
الأولى : أن يطلق لفظ «الإمكان» ويراد به الإمكان العام.
والثانية : أن يطلق ويراد به الإمكان الخاص.
والثالثة : أن يطلق لفظ «الشمس» ويعنى به الجرم الذي هو والرابعة : أن يطلق و يعني به الضوء اللازم.
الملزوم.
Topics of words. Whenever it is uttered, its meaning is understood by knowledge of its convention. And it is either correspondence, inclusion, or commitment. That is because if a word signifies a meaning according to convention, then that meaning which is the signification of the word is either the very meaning it was assigned for, or part of it, or external to it. So the signification of the word for its meaning by virtue of the word being assigned for that meaning is correspondence, like the signification of 'human' for 'rational animal'; for 'human' signifies 'rational animal' only because it is assigned for 'rational animal'. And its signification for its meaning by virtue of the word being assigned for a meaning within which that signified meaning is contained is inclusion, like the signification of 'human' for 'animal' or 'rational'; for 'human' signifies 'animal' or 'rational' only because it is assigned for 'rational animal', and 'animal' is a meaning contained in it. And its signification for its meaning by virtue of the word being assigned for a meaning from which that signified meaning is external is commitment, like the signification of 'human' for 'capable of knowledge and the craft of writing'; for its signification for it is by virtue of the word being assigned for 'rational animal', and 'capable of knowledge and the craft of writing' is external to it. As for naming the first signification 'correspondence', it is because the word corresponds—i.e., agrees with the whole of what it was assigned for—from their saying 'the sole corresponds to the sole' when they match. As for naming the second signification 'inclusion', it is because the part of the assigned meaning is included within it, so it is signification of what is within the assigned meaning. As for naming the third signification 'commitment', it is because the word does not signify every matter external to its assigned meaning, but only the external that is necessary to it. And the definitions of the three significations were restricted by the mediation of convention, because if they were not so restricted, the definition of some significations would be violated by others. That is because it is possible that a word is shared between the part and the whole, like 'possibility' (imkan), for it is assigned for specific possibility—which is negation of necessity from both sides—and for general possibility; and that a word is shared between the necessitated and the necessary, like 'sun' (shams), for it is assigned for the body and the light. From this four forms are conceivable: First: that the word 'imkan' is uttered and general possibility is intended. Second: that it is uttered and specific possibility is intended. Third: that the word 'shams' is uttered and the body which is the necessitated is meant. Fourth: that it is uttered and the necessary light is meant.
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage defines the three types of linguistic signification (dalala) in Islamic logic: مطابقة (correspondence), تضمن (inclusion), and التزام (commitment). The author begins by stating that whenever a word is uttered, its meaning is understood by knowledge of its convention (wad'). The signification is then categorized based on the relationship between the signified meaning and the original assigned meaning. If the signified meaning is exactly what the word was put for, it is correspondence, e.g., 'human' signifies 'rational animal'. If the signified meaning is a part of the original meaning, it is inclusion, e.g., 'human' signifies 'animal' or 'rational'. If the signified meaning is external to the original meaning but necessarily implied by it, it is commitment, e.g., 'human' signifies 'capable of knowledge and writing'. The author then explains the rationale for the names: 'correspondence' because the word matches the whole assigned meaning; 'inclusion' because the part is included within the whole; 'commitment' because only external necessary concomitants are signified, not any external. Finally, the author stresses that these definitions must include the condition 'by convention' (بالوضع) to avoid counterexamples where a word might be ambiguous (mushtarak) between a part and a whole, like 'imkan' (possibility) used for both general and specific possibility, or between a necessitated (malzum) and its necessary concomitant (lazim), like 'shams' (sun) used for both the celestial body and its light. Without the condition, the same word could be classified under different significations depending on the intended meaning. This safeguards the definitions from being violated.

Key Terms
مطابقة
تضمن
التزام
وضع

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Tadammun
C) Iltizam

Key Takeaway
The three types of signification are distinguished by the relationship between the signified meaning and the word's original assignment: whole, part, or necessary external.

6 min
The Necessity of the Condition 'by Convention' in Signification
Qutbi argues for the necessity of the condition 'بالوضع' in the definitions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the condition 'by convention' (bil-wad') is necessary in defining the three types of signification, using the examples of 'imkan' and 'shams'.

Core Idea
Without the condition 'by convention', ambiguous words would violate the definitions of signification types.

Qutbi introduces a crucial condition: the definitions of mutabaqa, tadammun, and iltizam must be qualified 'by convention'. This prevents counterexamples where a word has multiple assigned meanings and could be misclassified. He illustrates with the words 'imkan' (possibility) and 'shams' (sun), which are ambiguous between a part and whole or between a thing and its necessary concomitant.

Guided Path
1
Understand the problem of polysemy
A word like 'imkan' is assigned two distinct meanings: general possibility (part) and specific possibility (whole). Without the condition, using 'imkan' for general possibility might be misclassified as tadammun of specific possibility.
The same word has two separate conventions.
2
Recognize the violation without condition
If the condition 'by convention' is not applied, the definition of tadammun could be violated: a word that is mutabaqa for one meaning might be incorrectly seen as tadammun for another meaning that it was never assigned for in that context.
The word's signification must be tied to the specific convention intended.
3
Apply the condition to 'shams'
'Shams' is assigned for both the celestial body (malzum) and its light (lazim). Without the condition, saying 'shams' for the light could be considered iltizam of the body, but it is actually mutabaqa for the light by convention.
The condition ensures each use is evaluated based on its own convention.
4
Generalize the necessity
The condition protects the definitions from being violated by words that are mushtarak (shared between multiple meanings). It ensures that each signification type is determined by the actual conventional relationship for that specific meaning.
This is a key safeguard in Islamic logic.

As for naming the third signification 'commitment', it is because the word does not signify every matter external to its assigned meaning, but only the external that is necessary to it. And the definitions of the three significations were restricted by the mediation of convention, because if they were not so restricted, the definition of some significations would be violated by others. That is because it is possible that a word is shared between the part and the whole, like 'possibility' (imkan), for it is assigned for specific possibility—which is negation of necessity from both sides—and for general possibility; and that a word is shared between the necessitated and the necessary, like 'sun' (shams), for it is assigned for the body and the light. From this four forms are conceivable: First: that the word 'imkan' is uttered and general possibility is intended. Second: that it is uttered and specific possibility is intended. Third: that the word 'shams' is uttered and the body which is the necessitated is meant. Fourth: that it is uttered and the necessary light is meant.
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage defines the three types of linguistic signification (dalala) in Islamic logic: مطابقة (correspondence), تضمن (inclusion), and التزام (commitment). The author begins by stating that whenever a word is uttered, its meaning is understood by knowledge of its convention (wad'). The signification is then categorized based on the relationship between the signified meaning and the original assigned meaning. If the signified meaning is exactly what the word was put for, it is correspondence, e.g., 'human' signifies 'rational animal'. If the signified meaning is a part of the original meaning, it is inclusion, e.g., 'human' signifies 'animal' or 'rational'. If the signified meaning is external to the original meaning but necessarily implied by it, it is commitment, e.g., 'human' signifies 'capable of knowledge and writing'. The author then explains the rationale for the names: 'correspondence' because the word matches the whole assigned meaning; 'inclusion' because the part is included within the whole; 'commitment' because only external necessary concomitants are signified, not any external. Finally, the author stresses that these definitions must include the condition 'by convention' (بالوضع) to avoid counterexamples where a word might be ambiguous (mushtarak) between a part and a whole, like 'imkan' (possibility) used for both general and specific possibility, or between a necessitated (malzum) and its necessary concomitant (lazim), like 'shams' (sun) used for both the celestial body and its light. Without the condition, the same word could be classified under different significations depending on the intended meaning. This safeguards the definitions from being violated.

إمكان
شمس

The condition 'by convention' ensures that each signification type applies only to the intended conventional meaning, preventing ambiguity from polysemy.

What Is Mantiq?

The Condition of Lexical Assignment in Conformity Signification
Author refines the definition of mutabaqa signification to exclude tadammun and iltizam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the definition of dalalat al-mutabaqa requires the condition 'bi-wasitat al-wad'' and apply it to distinguish mutabaqa from both tadammun and iltizam.

Core Idea
Without the mediation condition, mutabaqa would swallow tadammun and iltizam.

In this passage, the author refines the definition of dalalat al-mutabaqa by adding a critical condition: that the signification must be directly by virtue of the lexical assignment, not mediated through another meaning. He demonstrates with two counterexamples from the words 'imkan' (possibility) and 'shams' (sun) that without this condition, tadammun and iltizam would erroneously count as mutabaqa. Understanding this refinement is essential for precise logical analysis in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of mutabaqa
The original definition is 'signification of the word for the entire meaning for which it was lexically assigned'. Note that it does not specify how the signification occurs.
2
Examine the counterexample for tadammun
When 'imkan' is used for specific possibility (imkan khas), it also signifies general possibility (imkan 'amm) by tadammun. Without the condition, one could say the general possibility is also mutabaqa because the word is assigned to it as well. The condition excludes it because the tadammun signification arises from the assignment to the specific possibility, not directly from assignment to the general.
The general possibility is part of the specific possibility.
3
Examine the counterexample for iltizam
When 'shams' is used for the celestial body, it also signifies light by iltizam. Without the condition, one could argue that light is also mutabaqa because the word is assigned to light (as it is a meaning of the word? Actually, the condition excludes it because the signification of light is not directly by assignment to light but by assignment to the body which entails light.
Light is a necessary concomitant.
4
Understand how the condition resolves both
By adding 'bi-wasitat al-wad'', we require that the signification be directly by the lexical assignment. In both cases, the problematic signification is mediated through another meaning, thus they are excluded.
5
Notice the symmetry with tadammun's definition
The author also shows that if tadammun were defined without the condition, it would be violated by mutabaqa. This underscores the necessity of precise conditions in definitions.

(۲) أي لتحقق تلك الدلالة التضمنية فإنّها ثابتة بواسطة وضع اللفظ للإمكان الخاص، ولا مدخل فيها لوضعه للإمكان العام، بل الوضع للإمكان العام بسبب دلالة أخرى عليه مطابقة (شريف). وأما الانتقاض بدلالة الالتزام فلأنه إذا أطلق لفظ «الشمس» وعني به الجرم كان دلالته عليه مطابقة، وعلى الضوء التزاماً، مع أنه يصدق عليها أنها دلالة اللفظ على ما وضع له، فلو لم يقيد حد دلالة المطابقة بـ«توسط الوضع»، دخلت فيه دلالة الالتزام، ولما قيد به خرجت عنه؛ لأن تلك الدلالة وإن كانت «دلالة اللفظ على ما وضع له» إلا أنها ليست بواسطة أن اللفظ موضوع له، لأنا لو فرضنا أنه ليس بموضوع للضوء، ماكان دالاً عليه بتلك الدلالة، بل بسبب وضع اللفظ للجرم الملزوم له. وكذا لو لم يقيد حدّ دلالة التضمّن بذلك القيد لانتقض بدلالة المطابقة، فإنّه إذا أطلق لفظ «الإمكان» و أريد به الإمكان العام كان دلالته عليه مطابقة، وصدق عليها أنها دلالة اللفظ على ما دخل في المعنى الموضوع له؛ لأنّ الإمكان العام دخل في الإمكان الخاص، وهو معنى اللفظ بإزائه أيضاً، فإذا قيدنا الحد بـ«توسط الوضع» خرجت عنه، لأنها ليست بواسطة أن اللفظ موضوع لما دخل ذلك المعنى فيه. (۱) يعني أن هناك دلالة مطابقيّة، وإن كان هناك أيضاً دلالة تضمنية لما عرفت، فتلك المطابقة تدخل في حد التضمن إن لم يقيد بذلك القيد، وإذا قيد فلا انتقاض (شریف). (۲) لما كان الضوء مشتملاً على جهتين : إحداهما كونه لازماً للمعنى الموضوع له - أعني الجرم - والثانية كونه موضوعاً له، فلفظ «الشمس» يدلّ عليه دلالتين : إحداهما مطابقة والأخرى التزام، ويصدق على هذه الدلالة الالتزامية أنها دلالة اللفظ على المعنى الموضوع له فينتقض حدّ دلالة المطابقة بالالتزام، فإذا اعتبر قيد التوسط لم ينتقض (شريف).
And if these forms are realized, we say: Were the definition of conformity signification not restricted by the condition 'mediation of the lexical assignment', it would be violated by implication and implicative signification. As for violation by implication: because if the word 'imkan' is used and the specific possibility is meant, its signification of the specific possibility is conformity and of the general possibility is implication, and it would be true of it that it is the signification of the word for what it was assigned to, because the general possibility is also what the word 'imkan' was assigned to. Thus implication signification would enter the definition of conformity signification and it would not be restrictive. And if we restrict it by the condition 'mediation of the lexical assignment', that signification exits from it, because the signification of the word 'imkan' for the general possibility in that form, although it is the signification of the word for what it was assigned to, it is not by virtue of the word being assigned for the general possibility — since it is realized even if we assume the absence of its assignment for it — but by virtue of the word being assigned for the specific possibility which includes the general possibility. (1) He means that the word 'imkan' when used for the specific possibility signifies the general possibility by implication, and that does not contradict its also signifying the general possibility by conformity, because two aspects meet in the general possibility: one is its being part of the meaning assigned to — namely the specific possibility — and the other is its being assigned to. So the word 'imkan' must signify it by two significations from those two aspects. If we consider its implicative signification, it would be true of it that it is 'the signification of the word for the entire meaning assigned to', and if we restrict the definition of conformity by the condition of mediation, that implicative signification exits from the definition of conformity (Sharif). (2) That is, because that implicative signification is established by virtue of the word's assignment for the specific possibility, and the assignment for the general possibility has no role in it; rather, the assignment for the general possibility is due to another signification upon it by conformity (Sharif). As for violation by implicative signification: because if the word 'shams' is used and the celestial body is meant, its signification of it is conformity, and of the light is implicative, when it would be true of it that it is the signification of the word for what it was assigned to. So if the definition of conformity signification were not restricted by 'mediation of the lexical assignment', implicative signification would enter it, and when we restrict it with it, it exits from it; because that signification, even if it is 'the signification of the word for what it was assigned to', it is not by virtue of the word being assigned to it, for if we assume it is not assigned to light, it would not be signified by that signification, but rather by virtue of the word's assignment for the celestial body which entails it. And likewise, if the definition of implication signification were not restricted by that condition, it would be violated by conformity signification: because if the word 'imkan' is used and the general possibility is meant, its signification of it is conformity, and it would be true of it that it is the signification of the word for what entered into the meaning assigned to; because the general possibility entered into the specific possibility, and it is also the meaning of the word in its own right. So if we restrict the definition by 'mediation of the lexical assignment', it exits from it, because it is not by virtue of the word being assigned to what that meaning entered into. (1) He means that there is a conformity signification, although there is also an implicative signification as you know, so that conformity would enter the definition of implication if not restricted by that condition, and if restricted, there is no violation (Sharif). (2) Because light has two aspects: one is its being necessary for the meaning assigned to — namely the celestial body — and the second is its being assigned to. So the word 'shams' signifies it by two significations: one conformity and the other implication, and it would be true of this implicative signification that it is the signification of the word for the meaning assigned to, so the definition of conformity signification would be violated by implication; if the condition of mediation is considered, it is not violated (Sharif).
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage is a logical refinement of the definition of dalalat al-mutabaqa (conformity signification). The author argues that without the qualifying phrase 'bi-wasitat al-wad'' (by mediation of the lexical assignment), the definition would incorrectly include both dalalat al-tadammun (implication signification) and dalalat al-iltizam (implicative signification). The explanation proceeds by giving counterexamples. For tadammun: The word 'imkan' (possibility) can mean either specific possibility (imkan khas) or general possibility (imkan 'amm). When used to mean specific possibility, it signifies the specific possibility by mutabaqa and the general possibility by tadammun (since the general is part of the specific). Without the condition, one could say that the signification of the general possibility is also mutabaqa because the word is assigned to the general possibility as well (i.e., it is also a meaning of the word). However, the condition 'bi-wasitat al-wad'' excludes this because the tadammun signification arises from the word's assignment to the specific possibility, not directly from assignment to the general. For iltizam: The word 'shams' (sun) signifies the celestial body by mutabaqa and light by iltizam (since light is inseparable from the sun). Without the condition, the light signification could be considered mutabaqa because the word is assigned to light also? Actually the text examines the reverse: Without the condition, iltizam would violate mutabaqa. But the key point is that the condition ensures that for mutabaqa, the signification must be directly by virtue of the lexical assignment, not mediated through another meaning. The passage also notes that similarly, the definition of tadammun must be restricted to avoid violation by mutabaqa. The commentator (Sharif) adds clarifications in parentheses. The arguments are rigorous and show the necessity of precise conditions in logical definitions.

What Is Mantiq?

Refining the Definitions of Signification: Mediation and Mental Concomitance
Author refines definitions of signification types and states condition for implicative signification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three types of signification using the condition of 'mediation of the conventional meaning' and explain the requirement of mental concomitance for implicative signification.

Core Idea
The types of signification are distinguished by whether the meaning is the placed meaning, a part of it, or an external necessary concomitant.

In this passage, the author refines the definitions of mutabaqa, tadhammun, and iltizam to prevent conceptual overlap. You will see how a simple restriction—tawassut al-wad'—ensures each definition captures only its intended type, and why implicative signification requires only mental, not external, concomitance. This foundational precision is vital for correctly analysing any word's signification in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types of signification and their basic definitions
Recall that mutabaqa is signification for the exact placed meaning, tadhammun for a part of it, and iltizam for an external meaning necessarily linked in the mind. Note that the author begins by addressing potential counterexamples to these definitions.
The basic definitions are given in earlier lessons; here they are refined.
2
Understand the problem: without restriction, definitions overlap
The author shows that without the phrase 'tawassut al-wad', the definition of mutabaqa would incorrectly include iltizam (e.g., 'sun' for light), and the definition of tadhammun would include mutabaqa (e.g., 'imkan' for general possibility). This is because in these cases, the signification is still 'for what the word was placed for' in some sense.
The examples: 'sun' placed for the celestial body, but used for light; 'imkan' placed for specific possibility, but used for general possibility.
3
See how the restriction 'tawassut al-wad' resolves the overlap
By adding 'mediation of the conventional meaning', mutabaqa requires that the signification be directly through the word's placement for that exact meaning. For tadhammun, the signification must be mediated by the whole placed meaning. For iltizam, the signification is not mediated by placement for the implied meaning but rather by the placed meaning's causal relation. This restriction cleanly separates the three.
The marginal notes (Sharif) elaborate on how the restriction works, especially for the 'sun' example.
4
Grasp the condition for implicative signification: mental concomitance, not external
The author states that iltizam requires that conceiving the named necessarily leads to conceiving the implied meaning in the mind (mental concomitance). External concomitance—i.e., that the implied meaning exists whenever the named exists—is not required. The example of 'blindness' implying sight illustrates this: blindness implies the absence of sight mentally, but in external reality, blindness does not coexist with sight.
This condition prevents infinite regress: without it, every word could signify countless unrelated meanings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الانتقاض بدلالة الالتزام فلأنه إذا أطلق لفظ «الشمس» وعني به الجرم كان دلالته عليه مطابقة، وعلى الضوء التزاماً، مع أنه يصدق عليها أنها دلالة اللفظ على ما وضع له، فلو لم يقيد حد دلالة المطابقة بـ«توسط الوضع»، دخلت فيه دلالة الالتزام، ولما قيد به خرجت عنه؛ لأن تلك الدلالة وإن كانت «دلالة اللفظ على ما وضع له» إلا أنها ليست بواسطة أن اللفظ موضوع له، لأنا لو فرضنا أنه ليس بموضوع للضوء، ما كان دالاً عليه بتلك الدلالة، بل بسبب وضع اللفظ للجرم الملزوم له. وكذا لو لم يقيد حدّ دلالة التضمّن بذلك القيد لانتقض بدلالة المطابقة، فإنّه إذا أطلق لفظ «الإمكان» و أريد به الإمكان العام كان دلالته عليه مطابقة، وصدق عليها أنها دلالة اللفظ على ما دخل في المعنى الموضوع له ؛ لأنّ الإمكان العام دخل في الإمكان الخاص، وهو معنى اللفظ بإزائه أيضاً، فإذا قيدنا الحد بـ«توسط الوضع» خرجت عنه، لأنها ليست بواسطة أن اللفظ موضوع لما دخل ذلك المعنى فيه. (۱) يعني أن هناك دلالة مطابقيّة، وإن كان هناك أيضاً دلالة تضمنية لما عرفت، فتلك المطابقة تدخل في حد التضمن إن لم يقيد بذلك القيد، وإذا قيد فلا انتقاض (شریف). (۲) لما كان الضوء مشتملاً على جهتين : إحداهما كونه لازماً للمعنى الموضوع له - أعني الجرم - والثانية كونه موضوعاً له، فلفظ «الشمس» يدلّ عليه دلالتين : إحداهما مطابقة والأخرى التزام، ويصدق على هذه الدلالة الالتزامية أنها دلالة اللفظ على المعنى الموضوع له فينتقض حدّ دلالة المطابقة بالالتزام، فإذا اعتبر قيد التوسط لم ينتقض (شريف). وكذلك لو لم يقيد حد دلالة الالتزام بتوسط الوضع لانتقض بدلالة المطابقة، فإذا أطلق لفظ «الشمس» وعني به الضوء، كان دلالته عليه مطابقة، وصدق عليها أنها دلالة اللفظ على ما خرج عن المعنى الموضوع له، فهي داخلة في حد دلالة الالتزام لولا التقييد بـ«توسط الوضع»، فإنه إذا قيد به خرجت عنه لأنها ليست بواسطة أن اللفظ موضوع لما خرج ذلك المعنى عنه. قلت: ما مر من التقييد في دلالتي التضمن والالتزام هو ما في ما عدا الشمسية. وأما في الشمسية فلم يقيد. ثم قال: يشترط في الدلالة الالتزامية كون الخارج بحالة يلزم من تصوّر المسمّى في الذهن تصوّره، وإلا لامتنع فهمه من اللفظ؛ ولا يشترط فيها كونه بحالة يلزم من تحقق المسمّى في الخارج تحققه فيه، كدلالة لفظ «العمى» على البصر مع عدم الملازمة بينهما في الخارج. أقول : لما كانت الدلالة الالتزامية دلالة اللفظ على ما خرج عن المعنى الموضوع له، ولاخفاء أنّ اللفظ لا يدلّ على كل أمر خارج عنه فلابد لدلالته على الخارج من شرط، وهو اللزوم الذهني - أي كون الخارج بحالة يلزم من تصوّر المسمّى في الذهن تصوّره، وإلا لامتنع فهمه من اللفظ؛ ولا يشترط فيها كونه بحالة يلزم من تحقق المسمّى في الخارج تحققه فيه، كدلالة لفظ «العمى» على البصر مع عدم الملازمة بينهما في الخارج. (۱) وهناك أيضاً دلالة التزامية لما عرفت، فتأمل (شريف). (٢) أي عن المعنى الموضوع له، وإلا لزم أن يكون كل لفظ وضع لمعنى دالاً على معان غير متناهية، وهو ظاهر البطلان (شریف) (٣) وأما الدلالة على المعنى الموضوع له - أعني المطابقة - فيكفي فيها العلم بالوضع، فإن السامع إذا علم أن اللفظ المسموع موضوع لمعنى فلابد أن ينتقل ذهنه من سماع اللفظ إلى ملاحظة ذلك المعنى، وهذا هو الدلالة المطابقية، وكذا إذا
As for the objection by implicative signification: because if the word 'sun' is uttered and the celestial body is intended, its signification of it is mutabaqa, and of light is iltizam, while it is true that it is signification of the word for what it was placed for. So if the definition of mutabaqa signification were not restricted by 'mediation of the conventional meaning', implicative signification would enter into it, and when restricted by it, it exits from it; because that signification, although it is 'signification of the word for what it was placed for', yet it is not by way of the word being placed for it, for if we assumed that it was not placed for light, it would not signify it by that signification, but rather due to the word's placement for the celestial body which necessitates it. Similarly, if the definition of tadhammun signification were not restricted by that restriction, it would be invalidated by mutabaqa signification: for if the word 'imkan' is uttered and general possibility is intended, its signification of it is mutabaqa, and it is true that it is signification of the word for what entered into the meaning placed for, because general possibility enters into specific possibility, which is also the meaning of the word corresponding to it. So when we restrict the definition by 'mediation of the conventional meaning', it exits from it, because it is not by way of the word being placed for what that meaning entered into. (1) That is, there is mutabaqa signification, although there is also tadhammun signification as you know, so that mutabaqa would enter into the definition of tadhammun if not restricted by that restriction, and when restricted there is no invalidation (Sharif). (2) Since light comprises two aspects: one being it is necessary for the conventional meaning - namely the celestial body - and the second being it is placed for it, the word 'sun' signifies it in two ways: one mutabaqa and the other iltizam, and this implicative signification would be true that it is signification of the word for the conventional meaning, so the definition of mutabaqa would be invalidated by iltizam; so if the restriction of mediation is considered, it is not invalidated (Sharif). Likewise, if the definition of implicative signification were not restricted by mediation of the conventional meaning, it would be invalidated by mutabaqa signification: for if the word 'sun' is uttered and light is intended, its signification of it is mutabaqa, and it is true that it is signification of the word for what is outside the conventional meaning, so it enters into the definition of implicative signification were it not for the restriction by 'mediation of the conventional meaning'; for when restricted by it, it exits from it because it is not by way of the word being placed for what that meaning is outside of. I say: What has passed of restriction in the two types of tadhammun and iltizam is what is in non-Shamsiyya texts. As for the Shamsiyya, it was not restricted. Then he said: It is required in implicative signification that the external meaning be such that its conception is necessarily obtained from the conception of the named in the mind, otherwise understanding it from the word would be impossible; and it is not required that it be such that its realization in external existence is necessarily obtained from the realization of the named in it, like the signification of the word 'blindness' for sight despite the absence of concomitance between them in external existence. I say: Since implicative signification is signification of the word for what is outside the conventional meaning, and it is no secret that the word does not signify every external thing, so for its signification of the external, a condition is necessary, and that is mental concomitance - i.e., that the external be such that its conception is necessarily obtained from the conception of the named in the mind; otherwise understanding it from the word would be impossible. And it is not required that it be such that its realization in external existence is necessarily obtained from the realization of the named in it, like the signification of the word 'blindness' for sight despite the absence of concomitance between them in external existence.
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition on the conditions and definitions of the three types of signification: mutabaqa (conformity), tadhammun (inclusion), and iltizam (implication). The author begins by addressing potential counterexamples that would arise if the definitions were not restricted by the phrase 'توسط الوضع' (mediation of the conventional meaning). He gives examples: the word 'sun' signifies the celestial body by mutabaqa and light by iltizam. Without the restriction, the iltizam signification could be mistakenly included in the definition of mutabaqa because it is also a signification of the word for what it was placed for (since the word 'sun' is placed for the celestial body, but here it is used for light which is not the placement). The restriction clarifies that mutabaqa requires direct mediation of the conventional meaning (i.e., the word is placed for that exact meaning). Similarly, for tadhammun (where a part of the meaning is signified), without the restriction, mutabaqa could be confused with tadhammun. The example is the word 'imkan' (possibility) which can signify general possibility (a part of specific possibility) by tadhammun, but if intended as the whole meaning, it would be mutabaqa. The restriction ensures that tadhammun requires the signification to be mediated by the word's placement for the whole meaning. Then the author turns to iltizam: without the restriction, if 'sun' is used for light, that is actually mutabaqa (since light is one of the placed meanings? Actually the text says 'sun' is placed for the celestial body, but if used for light, it is not by mediation? The argument holds that without restriction, such cases would invalidate the definition. The marginal notes (Sharif) add clarification. After these refinements, the author states the condition for iltizam: the external meaning must be such that conceiving the named necessarily leads to conceiving that external meaning in the mind. This is 'mental concomitance' (اللزوم الذهني). Importantly, external concomitance (i.e., that the external existence of the named entails the external existence of the external meaning) is not required. The example given is 'blindness' and 'sight': blindness implies the absence of sight, but in external existence, blindness does not coexist with sight; yet mentally, conceiving blindness involves conceiving the absence of sight (so there is mental concomitance). The author emphasizes that without this mental connection, understanding the implied meaning from the word would be impossible.

According to the passage, which condition is necessary for implicative signification (dalalat al-iltizam)?
A) The implied meaning must exist in external reality whenever the named exists.
B) The implied meaning must be a part of the conventional meaning.
C) Conceiving the named in the mind must necessarily lead to conceiving the implied meaning.
D) The word must be placed for the implied meaning directly.

Key Takeaway
The restriction 'tawassut al-wad'' distinguishes the three signification types, and implicative signification requires only mental concomitance, not external existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
1. Construct an example from usul al-fiqh where the same word has both mutabaqa and iltizam signification. For instance, consider the word 'hajj' (pilgrimage). Identify its mutabaqa meaning and one iltizam meaning that has mental concomitance but not necessarily external concomitance.
?

What Is Mantiq?
beginner
8 min
Condition for Implicative Signification: Mental Necessity, Not External Coexistence
Author defines condition for implicative signification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the condition required for a word to have implicative signification (dalala iltizamiyya) and distinguish mental from external implication.

Core Idea
Implicative signification requires mental necessity, not external coexistence.

In this passage, the author explains that for a word to signify something beyond its direct meaning, there must be a necessary mental connection between the primary meaning and the implied meaning. This lesson breaks down that condition and clarifies common confusions, such as requiring external coexistence. You will also see how this applies to polysemy and composite meanings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary meaning
Determine the meaning originally placed for the word (mawdu' lahu). This is the direct signification by conformity (mutabaqa).
2
Recognize indirect signification
If a word signifies something other than its primary meaning, it must be either by implication (iltizam) or by inclusion (tadmin). Implication requires a mental necessary link.
3
Apply the condition for implication
Verify that from conceptualizing the primary meaning, the implied meaning necessarily follows in the mind. This is the test for genuine implicative signification.
4
Distinguish mental from external implication
Note that the author explicitly rejects external coexistence as a requirement. Even if two things are always found together externally (e.g., smoke and fire), the linguistic implication is only valid if the mental link holds. Conversely, things that never coexist externally (e.g., blindness and sight) can still be linked if the mind necessarily associates them.
5
Handle polysemy and composite meanings
Understand that a word with multiple independent meanings signifies each by direct signification (mutabaqa), not by implication. For composite meanings, each part is signified by inclusion (tadmin), which automatically follows from the whole.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأمر الخارج لازماً لمسمّى اللفظ بحيث يلزم من تصوّر المسمى تصوره - فإنه لو لم يتحقق هذا الشرط لامتنع فهم الأمر الخارجي من اللفظ، فلم يكن دالا عليه. وذلك لأن دلالة اللفظ على المعنى بحسب الوضع لأحد الأمرين : إما لأجل أنه موضوع بإزائه، أو لأجل أنه يلزم من فهم المعنى الموضوع له فهمه ، واللفظ ليس بموضوع للأمر الخارجي؛ فلو لم يكن بحيث يلزم من تصوّر المسمى تصوّره لم يكن الأمر الثاني أيضاً متحققاً، فلم يكن اللفظ دالاً عليه ؛ ولا يشترط فيها اللزوم الخارجي وهوكون الأمر الخارجي [؟] علم أن ذلك اللفظ موضوع لمعان متعدّدة فإنّه عند سماعه ينتقل ذهنه إلى ملاحظة تلك المعاني بأسرها، فيكون دالا على كل واحد منها مطابقة، وإن لم يعلم أن مراد المتكلّم ماذا من بين تلك المعاني، فإن كون المعنى مراداً للمتكلم ليس معتبراً في دلالة اللفظ عليه، إذ هي - أعني دلالة اللفظ على المعنى - عبارة عن كونه مفهوماً من اللفظ، سواء كان مراداً للمتكلم أو لا. وأما الدلالة التضمنية فلا تحتاج أيضاً إلى اشتراط، لأن اللفظ إذا وضع لمعنى مركب كان دالاً على كل واحد من أجزائه دلالة تضمنية، لأن فهم الجزء لازم لفهم الكل، ولا يمكن أن يكون اللفظ موضوعاً لخصوصية معنى مركب من أجزاء غير متناهية حتى يلزم دلالة اللفظ الواحد على أمور غير متناهية دلالة تضمنية. ولا يمكن أيضاً أن يوضع لفظ واحد بإزاء كل واحد من معان غير متناهية بأوضاع غير متناهية، حتى يلزم كونه دالاً بالمطابقة على ما لايتناهى
The external matter is necessarily concomitant to the meaning of the word such that from conceptualizing the meaning its conceptualization necessarily follows - for if this condition is not met, understanding the external matter from the word would be impossible, so it would not be indicative of it. And that is because the signification of a word on a meaning according to convention is for one of two reasons: either because it is placed in correspondence with it, or because from understanding the placed meaning its understanding follows, and the word is not placed for the external matter; so if it were not such that from conceptualizing the meaning its conceptualization follows, the second reason also would not be realized, so the word would not be indicative of it. And external implication is not required, that is, the external matter being [concomitant] ... It is known that that word is placed for multiple meanings, for when it is heard, the mind moves to observe all those meanings, so it is indicative of each one by conformity, even if it is not known what the speaker intends among those meanings, for the meaning being intended by the speaker is not considered in the word's signification of it, since it - that is, the word's signification of the meaning - is an expression of it being understood from the word, whether intended by the speaker or not. As for implicative signification (tadminiyya), it also does not require a condition, because if a word is placed for a composite meaning, it is indicative of each of its parts by implicative signification, because understanding the part necessarily follows from understanding the whole, and it is impossible for a word to be placed for a specific meaning composed of infinite parts such that it would entail the signification of one word on infinite things by implicative signification. And it is also impossible that one word be placed in correspondence with each of infinite meanings with infinite conventions, such that it would entail it being indicative by conformity of what is infinite.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage defines the condition for dalala iltizamiyya (implicative signification). The author explains that for a word to signify an external matter (amr khariji) by implication, that external matter must be mentally concomitant to the word's primary meaning (mawdu' lahu). That is, conceptualizing the primary meaning must necessarily lead to conceptualizing the external matter. The reasoning is that a word signifies by convention either directly (as subject) or through implication. Since the word is not directly placed for the external matter, the only way it can signify it is if the external matter is a mental concomitant. The author then clarifies that this mental necessity (luzum dhihni) is sufficient; external coexistence (luzum khariji) is not required. The proof given is that if external coexistence were required, many valid implications (like 'blindness' implying 'sight') would fail. Then the author discusses polysemy: if a word is placed for multiple meanings, it signifies each by original (mutabaqa) signification, regardless of the speaker's intent. Finally, the author addresses tadminiyya (inclusion signification), noting it also requires no special condition beyond the word being for a composite meaning. The author argues against the possibility of infinite parts or infinite independent meanings leading to infinite significations.

Key Terms
دلالة الالتزام
اللزوم الذهني
اللزوم الخارجي
دلالة التضمن
دلالة المطابقة

Checkpoint
According to the author, in order for a word to have dalala iltizamiyya on something, what is the required relation between that thing and the word's original meaning?
A) The thing must always coexist externally with the original meaning.
B) Conceptualizing the original meaning must necessarily entail conceptualizing the thing in the mind.
C) The word must be explicitly placed for that thing as a secondary meaning.
D) The speaker must intend that thing.

Key Takeaway
For implicative signification, the necessary condition is a mental link, not an external one.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the word 'fire' (nar). Its primary meaning is the physical element. From conceptualizing fire, the mind necessarily conceptualizes heat. Does 'fire' have implicative signification on 'heat'? Apply the condition of mental necessity to decide, and explain why or why not.
?
