The Relations of the Three Significations: Definitions and Basic Relations
Commentator explains the relations and refutes claims of necessary implication.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three types of signification (mutabaqa, tadammun, iltizam) and explain why correspondence does not necessitate containment.

Core Idea
Correspondence does not entail containment because a word can signify a simple meaning with no parts.

In this passage, the commentator clarifies the logical relations between the three types of signification. Understanding these relations is crucial for analyzing how words convey meaning in Islamic sciences, from Quranic exegesis to legal reasoning. We will focus on the definitions and the key insight that correspondence stands alone, while containment and implication depend on it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three significations
From the passage, note the definitions: mutabaqa is signification for the whole meaning, tadammun for a part, iltizam for an external necessary concomitant.
These are standard definitions in Islamic logic.
2
Examine the relation between correspondence and containment
The passage states that correspondence does not necessitate containment because a word may be posited for a simple meaning (ma'na basit) with no parts. Thus, whenever correspondence is present, containment may be absent.
Containment requires the meaning to have parts.
3
Understand why containment and implication depend on correspondence
The commentator mentions that containment and implication cannot occur without correspondence, because the dependent (the part or the concomitant) cannot exist without the independent (the whole).
This is a logical dependency: the part presupposes the whole.
4
Recognize the condition for implication
Implication requires a mental necessary concomitant (luzum dhihni). The passage notes that it is not certain that every quiddity has such a concomitant, so correspondence does not necessarily entail implication.
This sets the stage for the refutation in the next part.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
معلوم، وماقيل: «إنّ تصوّر كل ماهيّة يستلزم تصوّر أنها ليست غيرها فممنوع؛ ومن هذا تبين عدم استلزام التضمن الالتزام.
وأمّاهما فلا يوجدان إلا مع المطابقة لاستحالة وجود التابع – من حيث أنه تابع - بدون المتبوع.
أقول : أراد المصنف بيان نسب الدلالات الثلاثة بعضها مع بعض بالاستلزام وعدمه، فالمطابقة لاتستلزم التضمن أي ليس متي تحققت المطابقة تحقق التضمّن لجواز أن يكون اللفظ موضوعاً لمعنى بسيط، فيكون دلالته عليه مطابقة، ولا تضمّن هاهنا، لأن المعنى البسيط لاجزء له، وأما استلزام المطابقة الالتزام، فغير متيقن، لأن الالتزام يتوقف على أن يكون لمعنى اللفظ لازم، بحيث يلزم من تصوّر المعنى تصوره، وكون كل ماهيّة بحيث يوجد لها لازم كذلك غير معلوم، لجواز أن يكون من الماهيات مالا يستلزم شيئاً كذلك، فإذا كان اللفظ موضوعاً لتلك الماهية كان دلالته عليها مطابقة، ولا التزام لانتفاء شرطه - وهو اللزوم الذهني. وزعم الإمام أنّ المطابقة مستلزمة للالتزام، لأن تصوّر كلّ ماهية يستلزم تصور لازم من لوازمها وأقله أنها ليست غيرها، واللفظ إذا دل على الملزوم بالمطابقة دلّ على اللازم في التصوّر بالالتزام.
وجوابه أنا لانسلّم أن تصوّر كل ماهيّة يستلزم تصوّر أنها ليست غيرها، فكثيرا ما نتصور ماهيات الأشياء ولم يخطر ببالنا غيرها - فضلاً عن أنها ليست غيرها - ومن هذا تبين عدم استلزام التضمن الالتزام، لأنه كما لم يعلم وجود لازم ذهني لكلّ ماهية بسيطة، لم يعلم أيضاً وجود لازم ذهني لكل ماهيّة مركبة، لجواز أن يكون من الماهيات
It is known, and what was said: 'Indeed, the conceptualization of every quiddity necessitates the conceptualization that it is not other than itself' is rejected; and from this it becomes clear that containment does not necessitate implication. And as for the two [containment and implication], they do not occur except with correspondence, due to the impossibility of the existence of the dependent—insofar as it is dependent—without the independent. I say: The author intended to clarify the relations of the three significations to each other in terms of necessitation and non-necessitation. Correspondence does not necessitate containment, i.e., whenever correspondence is realized, containment is not necessarily realized, because it is possible that the word is posited for a simple meaning, so its signification of it is correspondence, and there is no containment here, because the simple meaning has no parts. As for correspondence's necessitation of implication, it is not certain, because implication depends on the word's meaning having a necessary concomitant, such that the conceptualization of the meaning necessitates its conceptualization, and it is not known that every quiddity has such a necessary concomitant, because it is possible that among quiddities there are those that do not necessitate anything in this way. Thus, if the word is posited for that quiddity, its signification of it is correspondence, and there is no implication due to the absence of its condition—that is, mental necessary concomitance. The Imam claimed that correspondence necessitates implication, because the conceptualization of every quiddity necessitates the conceptualization of a necessary concomitant among its concomitants, the least of which is that it is not other than itself, and if the word signifies the subject of implication by correspondence, it signifies the necessary concomitant in conceptualization by implication. Its answer: We do not concede that the conceptualization of every quiddity necessitates the conceptualization that it is not other than itself; for often we conceptualize the quiddities of things while not conceiving of other things—let alone that they are not other than themselves. And from this it becomes clear that containment does not necessitate implication, because just as it is not known that every simple quiddity has a mental necessary concomitant, so too it is not known that every composite quiddity has a mental necessary concomitant, because it is possible that among quiddities...
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage is an analytical expansion by the commentator (likely Qutb al-Din al-Razi) on the relations among the three types of signification: correspondence (mutabaqa), containment (tadammun), and implication (iltizam). The discussion begins by rejecting a previous claim that conceptualizing any quiddity necessitates conceptualizing that it is not other than itself; this rejection is used to show that containment does not necessitate implication. The commentator then notes that containment and implication only occur together with correspondence, as the dependent cannot exist without the independent. He explains the author's intention: to clarify whether the three significations necessitate each other. Correspondence does not necessitate containment because a word can be posited for a simple meaning with no parts, so no containment. Correspondence's necessitation of implication is uncertain because implication requires a mental necessary concomitant, and it is not known that every quiddity has one; some may have no necessary concomitant. The Imam (likely Fakhr al-Din al-Razi) argued that correspondence does necessitate implication, claiming that every quiddity's conceptualization necessitates conceptualizing its necessary concomitants, the least being its distinctness from others. The commentator refutes this: we often conceptualize quiddities without thinking of others, let alone their distinctness. Hence, containment does not necessitate implication, and similarly, we cannot assume every composite quiddity has a mental necessary concomitant. The argument follows a logical progression: first establishing the definitions, then presenting the claim, and finally refuting it with a counterexample.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does correspondence not necessitate containment?

C) Because correspondence always includes containment.
D) Because containment and implication are the same.

Key Takeaway
Correspondence does not entail containment; a simple meaning has no parts, so only correspondence applies.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

What Is Mantiq?
advanced
10 min
Refuting the Claim of Necessary Implication from Correspondence
Commentator explains the relations and refutes claims of necessary implication.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the Imam's argument that correspondence necessitates implication and evaluate why it fails using the condition of mental necessary concomitant.

Core Idea
Not every quiddity has a mental necessary concomitant; therefore correspondence does not guarantee implication.

In this continuation, the commentator takes on a stronger claim made by Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi: that correspondence always necessitates implication because every quiddity, when conceptualized, forces the conceptualization of its distinctness from others. The commentator refutes this by pointing out that we often think of things without this concomitant thought. This lesson dissects that refutation and its logical basis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Imam's claim
The Imam (Fakhr al-Din al-Razi) argued that correspondence necessitates implication because conceptualizing any quiddity requires conceptualizing that it is not other things, which is a necessary concomitant. Therefore, the word for that quiddity signifies that concomitant by implication.
This is an attempt to show that every quiddity has a mental necessary concomitant.
2
Recall the condition for implication
Implication requires a mental necessary concomitant (luzum dhihni) such that thinking of the meaning forces thinking of the concomitant. The Imam claims that 'being not other than itself' is such a concomitant.
The condition is explicitly stated in the passage.
3
Analyze the refutation
The commentator rejects the claim by denying that the conceptualization of every quiddity necessitates conceptualizing its distinctness. He gives a counterexample: we often think of quiddities without ever conceiving of other things, let alone their distinctness.
This is an empirical counterexample that shows the conditional is false.
4
Extend the refutation to containment not necessitating implication
The same reasoning applies to containment: just as simple quiddities may lack mental necessary concomitants, composite quiddities may also lack them. Thus, containment does not necessitate implication either.
This follows by analogy from the lack of certainty about every quiddity having a necessary concomitant.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
معلوم، وماقيل: «إنّ تصوّر كل ماهيّة يستلزم تصوّر أنها ليست غيرها فممنوع؛ ومن هذا تبين عدم استلزام التضمن الالتزام.
وأمّاهما فلا يوجدان إلا مع المطابقة لاستحالة وجود التابع – من حيث أنه تابع - بدون المتبوع.
أقول : أراد المصنف بيان نسب الدلالات الثلاثة بعضها مع بعض بالاستلزام وعدمه، فالمطابقة لاتستلزم التضمن أي ليس متي تحققت المطابقة تحقق التضمّن لجواز أن يكون اللفظ موضوعاً لمعنى بسيط، فيكون دلالته عليه مطابقة، ولا تضمّن هاهنا، لأن المعنى البسيط لاجزء له، وأما استلزام المطابقة الالتزام، فغير متيقن، لأن الالتزام يتوقف على أن يكون لمعنى اللفظ لازم، بحيث يلزم من تصوّر المعنى تصوره، وكون كل ماهيّة بحيث يوجد لها لازم كذلك غير معلوم، لجواز أن يكون من الماهيات مالا يستلزم شيئاً كذلك، فإذا كان اللفظ موضوعاً لتلك الماهية كان دلالته عليها مطابقة، ولا التزام لانتفاء شرطه - وهو اللزوم الذهني. وزعم الإمام أنّ المطابقة مستلزمة للالتزام، لأن تصوّر كلّ ماهية يستلزم تصور لازم من لوازمها وأقله أنها ليست غيرها، واللفظ إذا دل على الملزوم بالمطابقة دلّ على اللازم في التصوّر بالالتزام.
وجوابه أنا لانسلّم أن تصوّر كل ماهيّة يستلزم تصوّر أنها ليست غيرها، فكثيرا ما نتصور ماهيات الأشياء ولم يخطر ببالنا غيرها - فضلاً عن أنها ليست غيرها - ومن هذا تبين عدم استلزام التضمن الالتزام، لأنه كما لم يعلم وجود لازم ذهني لكلّ ماهية بسيطة، لم يعلم أيضاً وجود لازم ذهني لكل ماهيّة مركبة، لجواز أن يكون من الماهيات
It is known, and what was said: 'Indeed, the conceptualization of every quiddity necessitates the conceptualization that it is not other than itself' is rejected; and from this it becomes clear that containment does not necessitate implication. And as for the two [containment and implication], they do not occur except with correspondence, due to the impossibility of the existence of the dependent—insofar as it is dependent—without the independent. I say: The author intended to clarify the relations of the three significations to each other in terms of necessitation and non-necessitation. Correspondence does not necessitate containment, i.e., whenever correspondence is realized, containment is not necessarily realized, because it is possible that the word is posited for a simple meaning, so its signification of it is correspondence, and there is no containment here, because the simple meaning has no parts. As for correspondence's necessitation of implication, it is not certain, because implication depends on the word's meaning having a necessary concomitant, such that the conceptualization of the meaning necessitates its conceptualization, and it is not known that every quiddity has such a necessary concomitant, because it is possible that among quiddities there are those that do not necessitate anything in this way. Thus, if the word is posited for that quiddity, its signification of it is correspondence, and there is no implication due to the absence of its condition—that is, mental necessary concomitance. The Imam claimed that correspondence necessitates implication, because the conceptualization of every quiddity necessitates the conceptualization of a necessary concomitant among its concomitants, the least of which is that it is not other than itself, and if the word signifies the subject of implication by correspondence, it signifies the necessary concomitant in conceptualization by implication. Its answer: We do not concede that the conceptualization of every quiddity necessitates the conceptualization that it is not other than itself; for often we conceptualize the quiddities of things while not conceiving of other things—let alone that they are not other than themselves. And from this it becomes clear that containment does not necessitate implication, because just as it is not known that every simple quiddity has a mental necessary concomitant, so too it is not known that every composite quiddity has a mental necessary concomitant, because it is possible that among quiddities...
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage is an analytical expansion by the commentator (likely Qutb al-Din al-Razi) on the relations among the three types of signification: correspondence (mutabaqa), containment (tadammun), and implication (iltizam). The discussion begins by rejecting a previous claim that conceptualizing any quiddity necessitates conceptualizing that it is not other than itself; this rejection is used to show that containment does not necessitate implication. The commentator then notes that containment and implication only occur together with correspondence, as the dependent cannot exist without the independent. He explains the author's intention: to clarify whether the three significations necessitate each other. Correspondence does not necessitate containment because a word can be posited for a simple meaning with no parts, so no containment. Correspondence's necessitation of implication is uncertain because implication requires a mental necessary concomitant, and it is not known that every quiddity has one; some may have no necessary concomitant. The Imam (likely Fakhr al-Din al-Razi) argued that correspondence does necessitate implication, claiming that every quiddity's conceptualization necessitates conceptualizing its necessary concomitants, the least being its distinctness from others. The commentator refutes this: we often conceptualize quiddities without thinking of others, let alone their distinctness. Hence, containment does not necessitate implication, and similarly, we cannot assume every composite quiddity has a mental necessary concomitant. The argument follows a logical progression: first establishing the definitions, then presenting the claim, and finally refuting it with a counterexample.

Checkpoint
What counterexample does the commentator use to refute the Imam's claim that every quiddity's conceptualization necessitates conceptualizing that it is not other than itself?
A) We often conceptualize quiddities without thinking of other things, let alone their distinctness.
B) Some quiddities are simple and have no parts.
C) The word's signification can never be by implication.
D) The Imam's argument is based on a false premise about simple meanings.

Key Takeaway
Implication requires a proven mental necessary concomitant; it cannot be assumed for all quiddities.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Evaluate the following claim: 'The word "Quran" implies its miraculous nature (i'jaz) by implication.' Using the condition of mental necessary concomitant from the passage, does every conceptualization of the Quran necessarily involve conceptualizing its miraculous nature? Provide a counterexample if possible.
?
Construct a refutation of the Imam's argument using a different example from Islamic thought: argue that conceptualizing 'angels' (mala'ika) does not necessarily involve conceptualizing that they are not other creatures.
